rel=\"noopener\">Sofja Kovalevskaja Award</a></span></span></span><span class=\"color_19\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"> from the Humboldt Foundation, and a </span></span><span data-packed=\"false\" style=\"top:;bottom:;left:;right:;width:801px;height:auto;position:;min-height:71px;pointer-events:none\" data-min-height=\"71\" class=\"txtNew\" id=\"comp-j43u8bj3\"><p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">10/2019:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">International Conference on Genomes and AI - From Packing to Regulation</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Together with GV Shivashankar I am organizing a conference at the intersection of machine learning and genome biology. Recent technological developments in genomics as well as rapid advancements in AI and machine learning provide exciting opportunities for integrating and exploiting the emerging vast amounts of imaging and sequencing data. This conference will bring together leading experts, early-career scientists and students to unravel the mechanogenomic codes that link genome architecture and function, thereby paving the way for novel disease biomarkers and therapeutic interventions. </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">We have an amazing list of invited speakers and are looking forward to your submissions for a short talk or poster presentation.&nbsp;&nbsp; [</span></span><a href=\"https://mbi.nus.edu.sg/events/2019-genomes-and-ai/\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://mbi.nus.edu.sg/events/2019-genomes-and-ai/\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">website</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">] [</span><a href=\"https://mbi.nus.edu.sg/wp-content/uploads/2019/06/Genomes-AI-flyer-04062019-withlink.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://mbi.nus.edu.sg/wp-content/uploads/2019/06/Genomes-AI-flyer-04062019-withlink.pdf\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">flyer</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">07/2019:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">SIAM Conference on Applied Algebraic Geometry</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Together with Sandra Di Rocco, I was the chair of the SIAM Conference on Applied Algebraic Geometry that took place in Bern, Switzerland. We had over 160 (!) minisymposia and were able to attract 850 (!) participants, nearly 2x (!) as many as in the last conference.&nbsp;If you missed some of the outstanding plenary talks, see the conference website. A huge thank you to my amazing co-chair Sandra Di Rocco and the local organizers, in particular Jan Draisma, for a great collaboration! &nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://mathsites.unibe.ch/siamag19/\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://mathsites.unibe.ch/siamag19/\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">website</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">06/2019:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Simons Investigator in the Mathematical Modelling of Living Systems</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">I received a Simons Investigator Award! A huge thank you to Steve Wright and Bernd Sturmfels for their continued support and their supporting letters! Also a big thank you to my group for their excellent work!&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://www.simonsfoundation.org/mathematics-physical-sciences/simons-investigators/simons-investigators-awardees/\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://www.simonsfoundation.org/mathematics-physical-sciences/simons-investigators/simons-investigators-awardees/\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">announcement</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">06/2019:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Graduation of my first PhD student</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Congratulations to my PhD student, Yuhao Wang, for earning his PhD! Yuhao came from Tsinghua University to Cambridge (MIT) for his PhD and is now going to the Statistics Laboratory at Cambridge (UK) for a short postdoc and then back to Tsinghua University to start his own group. What a great journey!&nbsp; [</span></span><a href=\"https://9892f3bc-6175-4233-bf0d-6b3fcbe16b20.filesusr.com/ugd/ebd6ba_e4ef52f34d314bf384c56d6042db9667.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"document\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">commencement</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">] [</span><a href=\"https://9892f3bc-6175-4233-bf0d-6b3fcbe16b20.filesusr.com/ugd/ebd6ba_9a1e735cea024e1ca210cd3e7f51ddbf.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"document\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">good-by lab lunch</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">06/2019:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Anchored causal inference in the presence of measurement error</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">We just uploaded a paper to the arXiv that was led by my undergraduate (!) student Basil Saeed in collaboration with my PhD students Anastasiya Belyaeva and Yuhao Wang. We consider the problem of learning a causal graph under measurement error, a highly relevant setting ingenomics with single-cell RNA-seq data being known to be highly zero-inflated. </span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Using method-of-moments estimators, we develop a provably consistent procedure for estimating the causal structur from corrupted observations on its nodes, under a variety of measurement error models. We demonstrate our method's performance through simulations and on real data, where we recover the underlying gene regulatory network from single-cell RNA-seq data. </span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Great work, Basil, Anastasiya and Yuhao!&nbsp; [</span></span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1906.00928\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1906.00928\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">].</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">06/2019:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Anchored causal inference in the presence of measurement error</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">In a paper that we just uploaded to the arXiv, we consider the problem of estimating an undirected Gaussian graphical model when the underlying distribution is multivariate totally positive of order 2 (MTP2), a strong form of positive dependence. Such distributions are relevant for example for portfolio selection, since assets are usually positively dependent. A large body of methods have been proposed for learning undirected graphical models without the MTP2 constraint. A major limitation of these methods is that their consistency guarantees in the high-dimensional setting usually require a particular choice of a tuning parameter, which is unknown a priori in real world applications. Interestingly, we show that an undirected graphical model under MTP2 can be learned consistently without any tuning parameters. This is achieved by a constraint-based estimator that infers the structure of the underlying graphical model by testing the signs of the empirical partial correlation coefficients. We evaluate the performance of our estimator in simulations and on financial data. Great job, Yuhao and Uma!&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1906.05159\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1906.05159\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">06/2019:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Presentations of my lab's work at ICML</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">My lab members will be giving various presentations of our work at ICML this year. My PhD student Karren and I will be giving talks on how to integrate and translate between different data modalities using autoencoders in the </span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><a href=\"https://sites.google.com/view/icml-compbio-2019/home\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://sites.google.com/view/icml-compbio-2019/home\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Workshop on Computational Biology</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">, my PhD student Adit will be presenting our work on memorization in overparameterized autoencoders in the </span></span><a href=\"http://deep-phenomena.org/\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"http://deep-phenomena.org/\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Workshop on Identifying and Understanding Deep Learning Phenomena</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">, and I will be presenting our work on causality in the </span><a href=\"https://graphreason.github.io/\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://graphreason.github.io/\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Workshop on Learning and Reasoning with Graph-Structured Representations</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">. Come find us at ICML!</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">05/2019:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Total positivity in structured binary distributions</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">We just uploaded a paper to the arXiv, where we study total positivity in exponential families, in particular in Ising models. We show that totally positive exponential families are convex and hence maximum likelihood estimation can be solved via a convex optimization problem. In addition, we show that for quadratic exponential families such as Ising models or Gaussian models, the distributions form a polyhedral cone, where the faces correspond to conditional independence relations. Hence total positivity acts as an implicit regularizer. We also extend Iterative Proportional Scaling to an algorithm for computing the MLE in Ising models under total positivity and apply it to a dataset in psychology, where standard methods could not be applied due to its high dimensionality. Thanks for another great collaboration, Piotr and Steffen!&nbsp; [</span></span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1905.00516\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1905.00516\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">04/2019:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Abdul Latif Jameel Clinic for Machine Learning in Health Grant</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">12/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Paper at ICLR 2019</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Congratulations to my PhD student Karren! Our paper on scalable unbalanced optimal transport using generative adversarial networks just got accepted to ICLR. In particular, have a look at the application to population modeling in single-cell RNA-seq data during zebrafish embryogenesis in the blastula and gastrula stages.&nbsp; [</span></span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1810.11447\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1810.11447\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">12/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">T</span></span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">wo papers at AISTATS 2019</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Congratulations to my students Raj, Chandler and Karren, and our collaborators at IBM, Karthik and Dmitriy! Our papers \"Budgeted experimental design for targeted causal structure discovery\" and \"Size of interventional Markov equivalence classes in random DAG models\" were accepted at </span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">AISTATS 2019.</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">12/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Presentations at NeurIPS</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Congratulations to my students Yuhao, Chandler and Anastasiya! They will be presenting their paper on the direct estimation of differences in causal graphs at NeurIPS later this month.&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1802.05631\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1802.05631\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">In addition, my student Adit will be presenting our work on interpretable neural networks for image classification at the Machine Learning for Health (ML4H) Workshop at NeurIPS.&nbsp; [</span></span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1705.08078\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1705.08078\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">10/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Predicting cell lineages by generative modeling and optimal transport</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Lineage tracing involves the identification of all ancestors and descendants of a given cell, and is an important tool for studying biological processes such as development and disease progression. However, in many settings controlled time-course experiments are not feasible, for example when working with tissue samples from patients. We just uploaded a paper to the bioRxiv presenting ImageAEOT, a computational pipeline based on generative modeling and optimal transport for predicting the lineages of cells using independent datasets from different stages of a cellular process. As a proof-of-concept, we applied ImageAEOT to nuclear and chromatin images during the activation of fibroblasts by tumor cells in engineered 3D tissues and in various breast cancer cell lines and human tissue samples, thereby linking alterations in chromatin condensation patterns to different stages of tumor progression. Importantly, ImageAEOT can infer the trajectory of a particular cell from one snapshot in time and identify the changing features to provide early biomarkers for developmental and disease progression.&nbsp;&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://www.biorxiv.org/content/early/2018/10/29/455469\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://www.biorxiv.org/content/early/2018/10/29/455469\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">bioRxiv</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">07/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Presentations at ICML</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Congratulations to my PhD students Karren and Raj! Their papers were accepted at ICML and selected for oral presentations. They will be giving their talks at ICML later this month.&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1802.06310\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1802.06310\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv:Karren</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]&nbsp; [</span></span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1803.05554\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1803.05554\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv:Raj</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">06/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Maximum likelihood estimation for totally positive log-concave densities</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">We just uploaded a paper to the arXiv where we study nonparametric density estimation under a strong form of positive dependence known as MTP2. Given n samples from a d-dimensional MTP2 distribution we show that the MLE exists and is unique with probability one already when n\u22653, independent of d. In addition, we show that the MLE is a tent function in many settings and can be computed efficiently using the conditional gradient method. Thanks for a great collaboration, Elina, Ngoc and Bernd!&nbsp; [</span></span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1806.10120\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1806.10120\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">05/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Joseph A. Martore Award for Exceptional Contributions to Education</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">I received a teaching award for designing the most popular class in IDSS.</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">05/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Abdul Latif Jameel World Water and Food Security Grant</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; [</span><a href=\"http://news.mit.edu/2018/j-wafs-fourth-round-seed-grant-funding-0525\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"http://news.mit.edu/2018/j-wafs-fourth-round-seed-grant-funding-0525\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">news article 1</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]&nbsp; [</span></span><a href=\"https://jwafs.mit.edu/research/projects/2018/novel-systems-biology-tools-improving-crop-tolerance-abiotic-stressors\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://jwafs.mit.edu/research/projects/2018/novel-systems-biology-tools-improving-crop-tolerance-abiotic-stressors\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">news article 2</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p>&nbsp;</p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">04/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">High-dimensional joint estimation of multiple directed Gaussian graphical models</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">We just uploaded a paper to the arXiv where we provide an algorithm together with high-dimensional consistency guarantees for learning a collection of directed Gaussian graphical models. This problem is of particular interest for learning gene regulatory networks based on gene expression data from different tissues, developmental stages or disease states. As a corollary we also obtain high-dimensional consistency results for causal inference from a mix of observational and interventional data. Great job, Yuhao and Santiago!&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1804.00778\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1804.00778\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">04/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Lay Summaries of our Recent Collaborations with the Shivashankar Lab at NUS</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">The Mechanobiology Institute at NUS published some great news articles describing the results from our collaboration with the Shivashankar lab on nuclear architecture, mechanogenomic codes and machine learning for early cancer detection.&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://mbi.nus.edu.sg/science-features/determining-genomic-architecture/\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://mbi.nus.edu.sg/science-features/determining-genomic-architecture/\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">news article 1</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]&nbsp; [</span></span><a href=\"https://mbi.nus.edu.sg/science-features/nuclear-biomarkers/\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://mbi.nus.edu.sg/science-features/nuclear-biomarkers/\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">news article 3</span></span></span></a><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">04/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Summer School on Graphical Models: From Mathematical Foundations to Biological Applications</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Together with Niko Beerenwinkel and Lisa Lambarti I am co-organizing a summer school on graphical models at ETH Zurich. The summer school covers models for high-dimensional data, causal inference from observational and interventional data, algebraic approaches to graphical models, and applications to genomics. The format is general lectures in the morning (given by Bernd Sturmfels, Jack Kuipers, Niko Beerenwinkel and myself) and specialized short talks by participants in the afternoon. Registration and abstract submission is now open.&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://www.bsse.ethz.ch/cbg/cbg-news/summerschool-2018.html\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://www.bsse.ethz.ch/cbg/cbg-news/summerschool-2018.html\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">website</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">03/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Nuclear Mechanopathology and Cancer Diagnosis</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">My joint review with Shiva on how defects in nuclear mechanotransduction can lead to cancer onset and the use of machine learning methods to identify abnormal nuclear morphology and architecture as early cancer biomarkers just appeared in </span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\"><span style=\"font-style:italic;\">Trends in Cancer</span></span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">.&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"http://www.cell.com/trends/cancer/fulltext/S2405-8033(18)30056-6\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"http://www.cell.com/trends/cancer/fulltext/S2405-8033(18)30056-6\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">journal</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">03/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Promotion to Associate Professor</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">From June onward I am Associate Professor!&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://stat.mit.edu/news/idss-faculty-member-caroline-uhler-promoted-associate-professor/\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://stat.mit.edu/news/idss-faculty-member-caroline-uhler-promoted-associate-professor/\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">news article</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">03/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Minimal I-MAP MCMC for Scalable Structure Discovery in Causal DAG Models</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">We just submitted a paper where we propose a new method for sampling from the posterior over causal networks with provable guarantees, which overcomes some of the computational limitations of current methods, which depend on the maximum degree of the underlying causal DAG. This is a real limitation&nbsp; in particular for biological applications, which are known to contain high degree hub nodes. Great job, Raj!&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1803.05554\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1803.05554\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">02/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Geometry of Discrete Copulas</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">We just uploaded a paper where we unify the theory of discrete copulas with generalizations of the Birkhoff polytope studied in discrete geometry. Great job, Elisa and Liam!&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1802.06969\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1802.06969\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">02/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Characterizing and Learning Equivalence Classes of Causal DAGs under Interventions</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">We just submitted a paper where we show that the equivalence classes of causal DAG models under soft and hard interventions are the same and provide an algorithm for learning the interventional equivalence class from a mix of observational data and data from soft interventions. This has important implications for genomic perturbation experiments, since our results imply that the causal information gained from the more invasive gene knockout experiments do not provide more causal information than the less invasive gene knockdown experiments. Congrats, Karren and Abigail!&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1802.06310\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1802.06310\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">02/2018:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Direct Estimation of Differences in Causal Graphs</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">We have uploaded a paper where we develop a method for directly estimating the difference of causal networks. This is particularly beneficial when the individual networks are large and complex, while the difference is small and sparse, as for example for gene regulatory networks in different disease states or for related cell types, etc. We applied our algorithm to single-cell RNA-seq data during the activation of T-cells. Great job, Yuhao,Chandler and Anastasiya!&nbsp; [</span><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1802.05631\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1802.05631\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span class=\"color_28\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></span></a><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">12</span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">/2017:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Machine Learning for Nuclear Mechano-Morphometric Biomarkers in Cancer Diagnosis</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Our paper, where we develop a convolutional neural net pipeline for detecting subtle changes in nuclear morphometrics of single cells and apply it to differentiate between normal and cancer cells just appeared in </span></span><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\"><span style=\"font-style:italic;\">Scientific Reports</span>. In particular, we propose an alternative to the graphical lasso that can be applied in high dimensions and does not require any tuning parameters. Great job, Liam and Yuhao!&nbsp; [</span><span class=\"color_28\"><a href=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1702.03530\" target=\"_blank\" data-content=\"https://arxiv.org/abs/1702.03530\" data-type=\"external\" rel=\"noopener\"><span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">arXiv</span></a></span><span class=\"color_19\">]</span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span class=\"color_19\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"wixGuard\">\u200b</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\"><span class=\"color_19\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\">&nbsp; </span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">01/2017:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span style=\"font-weight:bold;\">Exact Goodness-of-Fit Testing for the Ising Model</span></span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"font-size:6px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span style=\"font-size:6px;\">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></span></p>\n\n<p class=\"font_8\" style=\"margin-left:80px; text-align:justify;\"><span style=\"letter-spacing:0.05em;\"><span class=\"color_19\">Our paper appeared in the <span style=\"font-style:italic;\">Scandinavian Journal of Statistics</span>.
